    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8488064561759812792">The <i>New York Times</i> bestselling, darkly funny memoir of a young New Yorker's daring dual life—advertising art director by day, glitter-dripping drag queen and nightclub beauty-pageant hopeful by night—was a smash literary debut for Josh Kilmer-Purcell, now known for his popular Planet Green television series <i>The Fabulous Beekman Boys</i>. His story begins here—before the homema</span>
  <span id="freeText8488064561759812792" style="display:none">The <i>New York Times</i> bestselling, darkly funny memoir of a young New Yorker's daring dual life—advertising art director by day, glitter-dripping drag queen and nightclub beauty-pageant hopeful by night—was a smash literary debut for Josh Kilmer-Purcell, now known for his popular Planet Green television series <i>The Fabulous Beekman Boys</i>. His story begins here—before the homemade goat milk soaps and hand-gathered honeys, before his memoir of the city mouse’s move to the country, <i>The Bucolic Plague</i>—in <i>I Am Not Myself These Days</i>,  with “plenty of dishy anecdotes and moments of tragi-camp delight” (<em>WashingtonPost</em>).</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163788570?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/763271-nancy">Nancy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163788570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18301756251463049398"><b>Posted at <a href='http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2013/07/i-am-not-myself-these-days.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelf Inflicted</a> </b><br/><br/>I’m not much of a TV person and have never seen <i>The Fabulous Beekman Boys</i> or heard of Josh Kilmer-Purcell, retired drag queen. Still, I’m glad I found this little gem about two misfits in love. By day, Josh works for an advertising agency. At night, he lovingly and painstakingly transforms himself into Aqua, a 7-foot blonde beauty who carries goldfish around in her plastic boobs. His boyfriend, Jack, is a very well-paid escort known as “Aidan” to his clients, and lives </span>
  <span id="freeText18301756251463049398" style="display:none"><b>Posted at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2013/07/i-am-not-myself-these-days.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a> </b><br /><br />I’m not much of a TV person and have never seen <i>The Fabulous Beekman Boys</i> or heard of Josh Kilmer-Purcell, retired drag queen. Still, I’m glad I found this little gem about two misfits in love. By day, Josh works for an advertising agency. At night, he lovingly and painstakingly transforms himself into Aqua, a 7-foot blonde beauty who carries goldfish around in her plastic boobs. His boyfriend, Jack, is a very well-paid escort known as “Aidan” to his clients, and lives in a posh apartment building guarded by doormen. The two guys enjoy a routine life of reading the paper together and ordering lunch from the deli, while listening to Jack’s beeper go off and occasionally running into his unusual clients.<br /> <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The truth is, there’s no movie of the week about a drunk drag queen and a crackhead hooker in love. There never has been. It’s not the kind of thing people would care about. People would flip right by the channel, either unbelieving or uncaring. Who’s the good guy? Who’s the bad guy? Aren’t they both bad? If they didn’t get what they deserved by the first commercial, it’d be on to the breast cancer movie.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />You’re so wrong, Josh. Right from the first page, I cared. I loved reading about your transformation to Aqua. You reminded me of my little brother, who got a kick out of trying on my mom’s dresses and heels. Your work hours and lack of sleep exhausted me, reminding me of my own hectic days working full-time, part-time, taking classes, and still finding time to party. You also reminded me of a close friend who appeared to be the happiest person in the world to everyone else, but drowned his pain in vodka. I loved your crazy and dysfunctional relationship with Jack in a city that has no mercy, yet is a haven for those who are different, and I loved your friendship with Laura and your relationship with your supportive mom who didn’t know the difference between transsexuals and drag queens.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You know that if you want to have an operation that’s something you can talk about with your dad and me.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Your story was beautiful, honest, and hilarious. If it wasn’t so darn funny, I would have cried.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18301756251463049398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_99461825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99461825" />
    <a title="Nikki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3616022-nikki"><img alt="Nikki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271886736p2/3616022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99461825?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki" href="/user/show/3616022-nikki">Nikki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3616022-nikki?shelf=true-story">true-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3616022-nikki?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3616022-nikki?shelf=dark-comedy">dark-comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99461825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16401640901164184629">The story is summed up pretty well by the author near the end: “The truth is, there’s no movie of the week about a drunk drag queen and a crackhead hooker in love. There never has been. It’s not the kind of thing people would care about. People would flip right by the channel, either unbelieving or uncaring. Who’s the good guy? Who’s the bad guy? Aren’t they both bad? If they didn’t get what they deserved by the first commercial, it’d be on to the breast cancer movie.” But that's not really true</span>
  <span id="freeText16401640901164184629" style="display:none">The story is summed up pretty well by the author near the end: “The truth is, there’s no movie of the week about a drunk drag queen and a crackhead hooker in love. There never has been. It’s not the kind of thing people would care about. People would flip right by the channel, either unbelieving or uncaring. Who’s the good guy? Who’s the bad guy? Aren’t they both bad? If they didn’t get what they deserved by the first commercial, it’d be on to the breast cancer movie.” But that's not really true. I love that this story is about two people on the margins of society, two quote unquote freaks, two addicts, two pathetic fuckups who see themselves in each other and fall in love almost instantly. But the greatest thing about this book is that despite the neverending darkness of the plot and all the horrible physical and emotional atrocities described within –- it’s fucking hilarious. You’re laughing and wincing and tearing up in a perpetual cycle. You love the author and yet you’re also disgusted by him. You’re pulling for his relationship with Jack to work even though they’re obviously not good for each other. But the story wouldn’t go down so easily without the spoonfuls of humor. When Josh wakes up from a vodka-induced blackout to find himself on the subway, he thinks, “Some people might get obsessed with figuring out how they wound up on the F train in drag, with no bag and only one shoe. But that’s simply not my style. What’s done is done. I’m sure I had my reasons.” </span>
  <a data-text-id="16401640901164184629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189130514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13177207558146953743">I absolutely LOVED this book. Ad exec by day, infamous drag queen by night, Josh/Aqua meets the man of his dreams at a club one night. One problem: Jack, the man of his dreams, is a male escort. But for a while, Jack is more stable than Aqua. This is a simultaneously hysterical, insightful and heartbreaking book that I devoured in almost one sitting. And if for no other reason than a fairly detailed look into how a drag queen gets ready for a night out, this book is well worth your time.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132415822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jeff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/166787-jeff"><img alt="Jeff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222352072p2/166787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132415822?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff" href="/user/show/166787-jeff">Jeff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739468081" href="/book/show/250539.I_m_Not_Myself_These_Days">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132415822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11938992507851969741">I don't know if it's appropriate to describe an alcoholic drag queen's memoir of his relationship with a crack cocaine-addicted S&M male escort as "sweet," but that is one of the words I would certainly use to describe this fascinating, wry, and wonderfully told autobiography. Josh is a master storyteller whose quips and acumen are as sharp as his stilettos. I found myself laughing and, at turns, crying at the details of his life and his relationship, a passionate love affair that was somehow as</span>
  <span id="freeText11938992507851969741" style="display:none">I don't know if it's appropriate to describe an alcoholic drag queen's memoir of his relationship with a crack cocaine-addicted S&amp;M male escort as "sweet," but that is one of the words I would certainly use to describe this fascinating, wry, and wonderfully told autobiography. Josh is a master storyteller whose quips and acumen are as sharp as his stilettos. I found myself laughing and, at turns, crying at the details of his life and his relationship, a passionate love affair that was somehow as tender as it was damaged, as loving as it was abusive, as depraved as it was ... well, normal. The brilliance and strength of this book is that it provides an unapologetic look at the grotesquerie of human relationships. The grotesquerie is NOT because it's about a a drag queen and a male escort, but because it's about two people trying to find love, which is one of the hardest, most difficult, most confusing things two people can try to do. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer633725698284435399">“I Am Not Myself These Days” was a Kindle deal of the day. So I did a preview on Amazon and read the Prologue, which begins:<br/>======<br/>I’m freezing. The door to the balcony is wide open. The wind has blown the bedcovers completely off my feet, and the room is dark except for the faint orange glow from the skyline outside. I can’t feel my toes. On the forty-second floor, the wind never stops blowing. <br/><br/>My boyfriend is standing over me with a knife. Two nights ago, after he had come home from a three-day</span>
  <span id="freeText633725698284435399" style="display:none">“I Am Not Myself These Days” was a Kindle deal of the day. So I did a preview on Amazon and read the Prologue, which begins:<br />======<br />I’m freezing. The door to the balcony is wide open. The wind has blown the bedcovers completely off my feet, and the room is dark except for the faint orange glow from the skyline outside. I can’t feel my toes. On the forty-second floor, the wind never stops blowing. <br /><br />My boyfriend is standing over me with a knife. Two nights ago, after he had come home from a three-day crack binge, he decided that I could have the rest of the month to get my stuff together and move out of our, well his, penthouse. He then returned to his regularly scheduled cocaine programming and hadn’t come home since. Until now.<br /><br /> “Why’s the door open?” I ask. <br /><br />“I was getting ready to kill you and then jump off the balcony,” Jack says as calmly as if he were telling me what movie he was planning to see. <br /><br />“With that?” I gesture toward the Wüsthof chef’s knife in his hand. <br /><br />“Yeah.” <br /><br />“But I just got that for Christmas.” <br />====<br />I admit, this persuaded me to pay the $1.99 for the full book.<br /><br />I felt especially voyeuristic reading this memoir of an alcoholic drag queen / advertising artist and his often endearing relationship with a congenial high end S&amp;M prostitute. It is very entertaining and well written, and I found myself quietly chuckling a lot.<br /><br />I have to wonder, as I did with Augusten Burrough’s Dry, how an alcoholic can remember his days so clearly. I have two beers and I’m a little foggy on events. They are both successful in advertising. Maybe they are just good at using their creativity to fill in the blanks. No matter, though. It’s a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="633725698284435399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of drug-fueled and sex-driven memoirs that are also funny</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6185160-riya?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6185160-riya?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6185160-riya?shelf=drugs-are-bad-mmkay">drugs-are-bad-mmkay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6185160-riya?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585803675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2783555444299542101">When I first bought this book I was pretty sure it was a fictional story about a girl and her boyfriend who were both drug addicts but still were able to find humor in their daily lives. I was not completely right, but I wasn't too far off either: turns out, this is a memoir about a young alcoholic drag queen and his/her hot escort boyfriend who is unfortunately addicted to crack - so if this sounds intriguing so far (remember kids, this book will contain loads of drugs and sex and all things ba</span>
  <span id="freeText2783555444299542101" style="display:none">When I first bought this book I was pretty sure it was a fictional story about a girl and her boyfriend who were both drug addicts but still were able to find humor in their daily lives. I was not completely right, but I wasn't too far off either: turns out, this is a memoir about a young alcoholic drag queen and his/her hot escort boyfriend who is unfortunately addicted to crack - so if this sounds intriguing so far (remember kids, this book will contain loads of drugs and sex and all things bad and naughty), then I suggest you pick up this book because not only is this crazy tale true, but it is very entertaining and hilarious as well. If you are already feeling a bit queasy reading this, then I suggest forgetting you ever started reading this review, and get yourself a cup of hot chamomile tea and a Nicholas Sparks book and stay far, far away from this book!<br><br>Now - on to the review! (Warning: prepare yourself for many quotes; they were just so funny and good, it would've been a crime not to include them).<br><br>Josh - our narrator - is in his mid-twenties and has recently moved to New York. During the day he works in an ad agency while during the night he drinks copious amounts of vodka and performs in different clubs as "Aqua" - a seven feet tall buxom blonde who has clear plastic boobs containing goldfish! <br><blockquote>I have a helmet of blonde hair and armor of corset to protect me from all manner of dull people - dull people who do things like watch how much they drink.</blockquote><br>During one of his performances, Josh meets Jack, who is not only handsome, polite, and kind - but also a bit of a mystery.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416964ra/824127.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The mystery is solved one night when Jack brings Josh over to his ridiculously expensive and beautiful penthouse apartment where Jack curiously discovers a fat middle aged man on the floor of the foyer - tied up! This - it turns out - is just one of Jack's clients for Jack is a highly paid gay escort whose specialty is BDSM and humiliation. Josh is shocked and yet intrigued:<br><blockquote>I'm intrigued that there's a level of perversity even beyond my realm of expertise. Where have I been? I feel so uncool. Show me more of this party I've been missing.</blockquote><br>Josh is soon enveloped in the never-ending party of drugs, alcohol, and all things sexual. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416964i/824128.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>At first, this is fun, and Josh doesn't have any inhibitions:<br><blockquote>It makes me wonder, what's the point of thinking twice anyway? The only possible outcome of double thinking is that you invariably end up negating whatever it was motivating you in the first place. Forcing yourself to think twice about something is just admitting that somehow you are instinctively stupid, and that repetition is the only thing that will save you from yourself.</blockquote><br>Things get out of control, however, when Jack becomes more and more addicted to crack cocaine. At first he only smokes it with his clients but then his addiction progresses and he is soon taking off for days and going on weeklong crack binges. Josh is distraught but he is also in a vicious cycle of his own - drinking vodka from sunup to sundown. This is a really good book if you really want to know about what goes on in the mind of a person that is an addict. At one point, Josh even considers trying crack himself:<br><blockquote>Note to self: expand your drug repertoire. Maybe drinking's just gotten to be too much of a habit. Maybe I should try other things more often. This is my new resolution. Quit drinking. Get healthy. Just use drugs. Medicinally, strategically. Be less messy.</blockquote><br>So what is Josh to do: stay with Jack or leave him? Help Jack get sober or work on himself by trying to quit drinking first? Is there any hope for these two, or not? Now read this book and find out for yourself. This memoir is just - great. I loved it. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377475ra/732755.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2783555444299542101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_225014901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225014901" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199068-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274056963p2/1199068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225014901?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1199068-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225014901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17205766344798082696">Brief Description: Kilmer-Purcell’s first memoir (before the The Bucolic Plague) chronicles his days as a drag queen named Aqua and his doomed love affair with a crack addicted male escort who specializes in S&M. The relationship between Josh and his boyfriend Jack is the heart of the book, and it shines brightly before exploding into a supernova of pain, addiction and loss.<br/><br/>My Thoughts: Kilmer-Purcell seems to have lived enough lives to fill many memoirs. Although it was hard to reconcile the Jo</span>
  <span id="freeText17205766344798082696" style="display:none">Brief Description: Kilmer-Purcell’s first memoir (before the The Bucolic Plague) chronicles his days as a drag queen named Aqua and his doomed love affair with a crack addicted male escort who specializes in S&amp;M. The relationship between Josh and his boyfriend Jack is the heart of the book, and it shines brightly before exploding into a supernova of pain, addiction and loss.<br /><br />My Thoughts: Kilmer-Purcell seems to have lived enough lives to fill many memoirs. Although it was hard to reconcile the Josh in this book (alcoholic ad man by day and drag queen by night) with the bumbling but persevering gentleman farmer of his second memoir, his wickedly sense of humor and self-depreciation was instantly familiar. Frankly, I’m impressed that Josh survived the days chronicled in this book long enough to transform himself into one of the Beekman Boys. Although this memoir is often really funny and fascinating in a “let’s see how the other more flamboyant half” lives sort of way, it is also filled self-destructive behavior that I found both compelling and horrifying. (I must warn you that this book isn’t for everyone. If graphic descriptions of gay sex, S&amp;M, or drug use offends your sensibilities, steer clear!) Although Jack and Josh don’t live anything near a conventional lifestyle, their love affair feels doomed in a tragic Romeo and Juliet sort of way. And just because the heart being broken belongs to a 6-foot drag queen who keeps live goldfish in his corset doesn’t make this story any less affecting, emotional or touching.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17205766344798082696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229187896" />
    <a title="Jack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1847852-jack"><img alt="Jack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595787248p2/1847852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229187896?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack" href="/user/show/1847852-jack">Jack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229187896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16367923534571047744">A memoir that is in equal measure appealing and appalling. Josh takes through a rabbit hole where drag queens live with $300/hour male escorts in penthouse apartments on the Upper East Side. Ad agency art director by day, drag queen by night, alcoholic throughout - and strangely, madly in love with Jack, a male hooker with a dedicated clientele and a remarkably lax building staff. Parties go on for days, with orgies and crack and hog-tied British CEOs waiting in the front hall when our hero(ine)</span>
  <span id="freeText16367923534571047744" style="display:none">A memoir that is in equal measure appealing and appalling. Josh takes through a rabbit hole where drag queens live with $300/hour male escorts in penthouse apartments on the Upper East Side. Ad agency art director by day, drag queen by night, alcoholic throughout - and strangely, madly in love with Jack, a male hooker with a dedicated clientele and a remarkably lax building staff. Parties go on for days, with orgies and crack and hog-tied British CEOs waiting in the front hall when our hero(ine) gets home from a hard night of vodka and vivacity.<br /><br />It's all rather remarkable, as a slice of la vie boheme of the turn of last century - life is the fastest of lanes. <br /><br />The extraordinarily detailed description of the ritual transformation from Josh to Aquadisiac - the shows, the shaving, the (ahem) "specialty attire," is actually riveting. <br /><br />Depending on your enthusiasm, or even your patience, for these hugely self-destructive people, Kilmer-Purcell's story is certainly unique. It's entertaining, or more fascinating, the way that train wrecks are. <br /><br />It's also written in a breezy style that goes down as easy as the chilled vodka our author swills night and day. Event at 300 pages, I finished it all in a few hours. Perhaps a bit too much like brunch - decadent, indulgent, and drinking early in the day. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16367923534571047744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_706488467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=gaymance">gaymance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=iffy-wiffy-sun">iffy-wiffy-sun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=eyebrow-quirk">eyebrow-quirk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=gritty">gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=what-the-bloody-fuck">what-the-bloody-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706488467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17836508295787186307"><b>An appalling and mesmerising train wreck and beautifully tragic.</b><br/> <br/><i>I Am Not Myself These Days</i> is a raw and powerful glimpse into Josh Kilmer-Purcell's life, rich with humour, vodka and glittered drag queens. Through the eyes of Josh and his drag queen counterpart, Aqua, a story of horrific, cringe-worthy wince-inducing fuck ups is told, laced with even more fucked up humour. And although I did not entirely enjoy Kilmer's prose at times, I could not tear my eyes away, even through the involuntary f</span>
  <span id="freeText17836508295787186307" style="display:none"><b>An appalling and mesmerising train wreck and beautifully tragic.</b><br /> <br /><i>I Am Not Myself These Days</i> is a raw and powerful glimpse into Josh Kilmer-Purcell's life, rich with humour, vodka and glittered drag queens. Through the eyes of Josh and his drag queen counterpart, Aqua, a story of horrific, cringe-worthy wince-inducing fuck ups is told, laced with even more fucked up humour. And although I did not entirely enjoy Kilmer's prose at times, I could not tear my eyes away, even through the involuntary flinches that came as the story unravelled. But above all that, it was the painfully, beautifully destructive love between the misfits that were Josh, Aqua and Jack that truly enthralled me. The three of them stole my heart and broke it; even as I cradle the shattered, jagged pieces, I know that I will never forget the love that was formed and eternalised in the glittering high rises and square square boxes of New York City.<br /> <br /><b>Rating:</b> I cannot help but flounder in this section. I did not enjoy it-- it gave me little joy-- but it hypnotised me and swept me away and crushed me. So I will leave with a tenuous 3.5 stars, but that rating is as inconsistent as the flickering starlight scattered across the night sky.<br /> <br /> Edit: *groan* I slip into purple prose when I'm emotional... Sorry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17836508295787186307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2883704910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2883704910" />
    <a title="Alexis Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19022440-alexis-hall"><img alt="Alexis Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533751057p2/19022440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2883704910?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexis Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexis Hall" href="/user/show/19022440-alexis-hall">Alexis Hall</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19022440-alexis-hall?shelf=rare-deviations-into-nonfiction">rare-deviations-into-nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19022440-alexis-hall?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19022440-alexis-hall?shelf=now-i-am-rather-sad">now-i-am-rather-sad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2883704910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12919256390704074064">Wow, this was awful. Awfully sad and awfully funny. And I liked it awfully. Like The Lessons above it’s a familiar story—this time the subgenre ‘being fucked up with another fuck up’—but, to my mind, it was a lot more successful. Because while “I’m messed up and I’m in love with someone messed up and no matter how hard we try we keep messing each other up” is familiar ground for a memoir, especially a queer memoir, the devil is in the details.<br/><br/>Set in New York in the 90s, Kilmer Purcell works as a</span>
  <span id="freeText12919256390704074064" style="display:none">Wow, this was awful. Awfully sad and awfully funny. And I liked it awfully. Like The Lessons above it’s a familiar story—this time the subgenre ‘being fucked up with another fuck up’—but, to my mind, it was a lot more successful. Because while “I’m messed up and I’m in love with someone messed up and no matter how hard we try we keep messing each other up” is familiar ground for a memoir, especially a queer memoir, the devil is in the details.<br /><br />Set in New York in the 90s, Kilmer Purcell works as an advertising executive by day. By night, he performs as his alter-ego Aquadisiac. Though, mainly he drinks. Then he meets an escort called Jack, who keeps a penthouse apartment and helps Josh bring his life fleetingly into some kind of order. And, of course, it unravels with Jack spiralling into drug addiction, and then both of them falling apart together.<br /><br />Despite the fact that the narrative has one direction, and the direction is down, I still found this really readable: it’s defiant and cynical and unsentimental and charming. I sometimes struggle with memoirs that want to wring a structure from the chaos of being alive. To me, it can feel too neat, too much like fiction. Not everything has meaning, a lesson to learn, a conclusion to find. IANMTD, by contrast, is very much about a particular time and a particular place—the legacy of something real, half-revealed and half-concealed by the artifice surrounding it. If it is “about” anything, I’d say it’s about love. Not in the sweeping romance, HEA way. But love as a thing that happens to you. The ways it changes you and the ways it doesn’t. All the ghosts we leave behind us of the people we were when we were in love.<br /><br />The last chapter, in particular… eeesh. Left me full of unexpected feels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12919256390704074064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Hallman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Hallman" href="/user/show/5292886-david-hallman">David Hallman</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3422096722116439571">Vodka. <br/><br/>To be candid, vodka is one of the reasons that I like Josh Kilmer-Purcell's "I am not myself these days." The central character, curiously enough named Josh, likes vodka. Well, more accurately, it's Aqua who LOVES vodka. Aqua...sorry, I didn't introduce her properly...Aquadisiac, but everyone calls her Aqua, is really Josh. Or Josh is really Aqua. How does it work with drag queens? Who is who?<br/><br/>Anyway, vodka figures prominently in "I am not myself these days" because it figures prominently </span>
  <span id="freeText3422096722116439571" style="display:none">Vodka. <br /><br />To be candid, vodka is one of the reasons that I like Josh Kilmer-Purcell's "I am not myself these days." The central character, curiously enough named Josh, likes vodka. Well, more accurately, it's Aqua who LOVES vodka. Aqua...sorry, I didn't introduce her properly...Aquadisiac, but everyone calls her Aqua, is really Josh. Or Josh is really Aqua. How does it work with drag queens? Who is who?<br /><br />Anyway, vodka figures prominently in "I am not myself these days" because it figures prominently in Aqua's life.<br /><br />Almost as prominently as Jack figures in Aqua's life. And who would not like Jack? Hot, sexy, muscular, very well-hung, Jack. Two things you need to know about Jack. He's deeply in love with Aqua (go figure) and he's a very successful male prostitute. Successful enough to have a stunning condo on a high floor in a classy Manhattan building in which there are drawers stuffed with large-denomination bills. I guess there's been some issue about folks in Jack's profession and the IRS. But I digress.<br /><br />Vodka, Aqua, Jack - that's pretty much the plot. Along with some white powdery stuff that Jack apparently loves a great deal. Almost as much as he loves Aqua. And that becomes an issue because Aqua isn't too keen on being the other woman to Jack's white vixen.<br /><br />You've got to read "I am not myself these days" if you like to laugh and cry and drink vodka. If you don't like to laugh and cry and drink vodka, read something else.<br /><br />* * *<br /><br />For information on "I Am Not Myself These Days: A Memoir" see: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/QS3I7D">http://amzn.to/QS3I7D</a><br /><br />For information on my memoir "August Farewell" and my novel "Searching for Gilead", see my website at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://DavidGHallman.com">http://DavidGHallman.com</a> <br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_103706238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103706238" />
    <a title="Badly Drawn Girl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3131165-badly-drawn-girl"><img alt="Badly Drawn Girl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263101002p2/3131165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103706238?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Badly Drawn Girl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Badly Drawn Girl" href="/user/show/3131165-badly-drawn-girl">Badly Drawn Girl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103706238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2569209451943914610"><br/>I picked this book up expecting to read wild stories about being a drag queen. I was imagining David Sedaris in drag. What I got was something much more moving and thoughtful. Yes, there are plenty of wild stories and hilarious anecdotes about Aqua, the author's other personality. But this is also a story about a doomed love affair, and the affect drugs can have on a relationship. Josh Kilmer-Purcell strikes the perfect balance, never allowing the laughs to obscure the reality of the painful rel</span>
  <span id="freeText2569209451943914610" style="display:none"><br />I picked this book up expecting to read wild stories about being a drag queen. I was imagining David Sedaris in drag. What I got was something much more moving and thoughtful. Yes, there are plenty of wild stories and hilarious anecdotes about Aqua, the author's other personality. But this is also a story about a doomed love affair, and the affect drugs can have on a relationship. Josh Kilmer-Purcell strikes the perfect balance, never allowing the laughs to obscure the reality of the painful relationship he found himself in, but also avoiding the all too common "after-school special" over-emotional portrayal of addiction. I went in expecting a light, funny but ultimately forgettable read but when I finished the last page I realized that I had gotten much more than I bargained for. This is a book I won't soon forget. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2569209451943914610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2547728604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2547728604" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8527195-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584674557p2/8527195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2547728604?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/8527195-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2547728604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6095578321604198919">Were this a fictional story, I don't think it would hold up very well - too much reliance on the shock value of excessive sex, drugs, and alcohol without much real narrative. It would have seemed like self-indulgent vice porn. But the fact that this is a true story (even assuming a generous amount of embellishment), that this world existed and likely still exists, makes this a mind-blowing memoir.<br/><br/>The book is effectively a snapshot of Kilmer-Purcell's life during his first year or so in New York.</span>
  <span id="freeText6095578321604198919" style="display:none">Were this a fictional story, I don't think it would hold up very well - too much reliance on the shock value of excessive sex, drugs, and alcohol without much real narrative. It would have seemed like self-indulgent vice porn. But the fact that this is a true story (even assuming a generous amount of embellishment), that this world existed and likely still exists, makes this a mind-blowing memoir.<br /><br />The book is effectively a snapshot of Kilmer-Purcell's life during his first year or so in New York. Rather than having a clear beginning, middle, and end, the book feels more like a collection of vignettes which seem to have only tenuous connections to each other - a deliberate effort on the author's part to recreate the vodka-induced fogs that served as interludes between the events of his days and nights. Kilmer-Purcell's use of language to convey his never-sober state of mind is one of the strengths of this book - the reader is often unsure of what exactly is happening, because the narrator often feels exactly the same way.<br /><br />The world Kilmer-Purcell describes is (at least for those of us not well-acquainted with drag queens and hookers) endlessly fascinating. How long does it take a drag queen to get ready for a show? How much money can you make as a hooker? How do you handle waking up in a stranger's apartment, or on a subway train, with no knowledge of where you are or how you got there? How do you dispose of a semi-conscious body? What do you say when your boyfriend says he's going to murder you? This book provides answers to these (and other!) burning questions we've all asked at some point.<br /><br />Not to be neglected is the "Finding Jack" section after the epilogue, which gives a brief yet satisfying update nine years after the events of the book, and which really should have been included as its own post-epilogue chapter.<br /><br />This book is hilarious and graphic and tragic and romantic and horrifying and a solid read for anyone who doesn't get offended too easily.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6095578321604198919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21089673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21089673" />
    <a title="Mr. Nickler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1119923-mr-nickler"><img alt="Mr. Nickler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209406437p2/1119923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21089673?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mr. Nickler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mr. Nickler" href="/user/show/1119923-mr-nickler">Mr. Nickler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Very much so.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21089673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6420589385255044234">I found this book at Unabridged (a neighborhood book store here in Chicago) and it had a review posted bookshelf that stated, if you like David Sedaris or Augusten Burroughs, you will probably enjoy this book as well. Based on that description I assumed I would like this book, but doubted the author could live up to the formers's works. While there are simalarites, between the three this book has in entirely different feel. The book is moving in a very unexpected way. While it is often very funn</span>
  <span id="freeText6420589385255044234" style="display:none">I found this book at Unabridged (a neighborhood book store here in Chicago) and it had a review posted bookshelf that stated, if you like David Sedaris or Augusten Burroughs, you will probably enjoy this book as well. Based on that description I assumed I would like this book, but doubted the author could live up to the formers's works. While there are simalarites, between the three this book has in entirely different feel. The book is moving in a very unexpected way. While it is often very funny, it also remains touching and hopeful. The love affair is very universal which is of course a surprise for me when I read it, seeing as I have never been in love with a crack addicted prostitute. The relationship between the two characters of the book transcend, gender, sexuality, and circumstance. <br /><br />This book deals with a specific section of gay life, but does so in way that allows the book to not feel like the other typical LGBT fanfare. The book is smart, and at times for me startling realistic. I related to this story on many levels but the authors drinking problem was probably the most resounding with me. Many books talk about problem drinkers, but so often I don't connect with other people's drinking problems. In this book I felt as if the author was writing my drinking story, and believe that only happens because the author is so honest and candid. <br /><br />The book is an easy read, and I would eagerly buy the authors next book.<br /><br />Matthew Nickelr</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1206476147" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206476147" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12831990-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571512255p2/12831990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206476147?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/12831990-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206476147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1555658646631690774">A memoir that will make you laugh at the most awful of moments. The love story of a hilarious alcoholic drag queen living day to day and a well paid male hooker who specializes is sadism and dapples with crack. Who wouldn't find that compelling? <br/><br/>This is a book that at any moment, especially in the most difficult and depressingly sad ones, can shock you into raucous bursts of laughter. It's Kilmer-Purcell's darkly self-deprecating comedic dialogue that make this tragic storyline, and it's dynamic</span>
  <span id="freeText1555658646631690774" style="display:none">A memoir that will make you laugh at the most awful of moments. The love story of a hilarious alcoholic drag queen living day to day and a well paid male hooker who specializes is sadism and dapples with crack. Who wouldn't find that compelling? <br /><br />This is a book that at any moment, especially in the most difficult and depressingly sad ones, can shock you into raucous bursts of laughter. It's Kilmer-Purcell's darkly self-deprecating comedic dialogue that make this tragic storyline, and it's dynamic duo of lovers, absolutely irresistible. I found myself yelling at our narrator and shaking my head, but reading on and hoping it would somehow keep going, and perhaps even have a happy ending. I was routing for this complicated, self-destructive drag queen, but it's hard to see any way that the story could conclude in anything besides disappointment and potentially complete disaster. This book manages to convey extreme depth within it's characters. Josh shows sadness and vulnerability throughout, but does it in such a way that you ravenously need to keep reading it - not an easy thing to accomplish. <br /><br />Simply written, but it needs absolutely nothing further. It's bare bones story telling with sequined dialogue that keeps you surprised. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1555658646631690774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_185734978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185734978" />
    <a title="Yvonne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4812701-yvonne"><img alt="Yvonne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373222956p2/4812701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185734978?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yvonne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yvonne" href="/user/show/4812701-yvonne">Yvonne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739468081" href="/book/show/250539.I_m_Not_Myself_These_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4812701-yvonne?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185734978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4846433824452899458">What's a memoir without lots of sex, alcohol & drugs. Well it certainly wouldn't be this one. We don't get a bio of Josh's life but more of a time period in his life when he first moved to New York city working at an advertising agency and moonlighting as Aqua, a drag queen who wears live goldfish on her breast (you have to read to find out how) & his love affair with Jack, a crack addicted S&M male escort. We follow the trajectory of this inevitably doomed relationship (hopefully this isn't a s</span>
  <span id="freeText4846433824452899458" style="display:none">What's a memoir without lots of sex, alcohol &amp; drugs. Well it certainly wouldn't be this one. We don't get a bio of Josh's life but more of a time period in his life when he first moved to New York city working at an advertising agency and moonlighting as Aqua, a drag queen who wears live goldfish on her breast (you have to read to find out how) &amp; his love affair with Jack, a crack addicted S&amp;M male escort. We follow the trajectory of this inevitably doomed relationship (hopefully this isn't a spoiler as Josh does dedicate the book to his current partner of 10 years Brent). Josh spares nothing in the telling of this story, &amp; some of it is quite ugly. The book however, is not depressing. It's quite hilarious in spots. As Aqua, Josh is the consummate entertainer. He carries that skill with him as a writer as well. This is funny, poignant, silly &amp; leaves you with many questions (like how can a man who is barely ever sober manage not just one but two careers fairly competently &amp; how can a romance between a drag queen &amp; a prostitute be so sweet). I'm not sure of the answers but I did enjoy the ride. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4846433824452899458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_43526232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/43526232" />
    <a title="Deb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1820344-deb"><img alt="Deb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232334644p2/1820344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43526232?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb" href="/user/show/1820344-deb">Deb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1820344-deb?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43526232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1994126011637135048">This memoir is delightful. Of course it has serious themes, but the context is so unique and refreshing that the drama of it is a perfect contrast. In this book, Kilmer-Purcell describes his transition in life from a flamboyant drag-queen to a more normal, functional adult. It is not for a reader that is homophobic, but most people should find the situations he finds himself in to be unusual (perhaps) but digestable.<br/><br/>What I particularly appreciated about this memoir is that, while the author is g</span>
  <span id="freeText1994126011637135048" style="display:none">This memoir is delightful. Of course it has serious themes, but the context is so unique and refreshing that the drama of it is a perfect contrast. In this book, Kilmer-Purcell describes his transition in life from a flamboyant drag-queen to a more normal, functional adult. It is not for a reader that is homophobic, but most people should find the situations he finds himself in to be unusual (perhaps) but digestable.<br /><br />What I particularly appreciated about this memoir is that, while the author is gay, the themes of the book are universally human. We all have to make hard choices about our lives, discover what love means, and how to evaluate ourselves. Kilmer-Purcell tackles these daunting tasks with a sense of humor that left me laughing outloud. (One particular episode includes a time where his boyfriend was threatening to stab him in the chest, and all he could seriously contemplate was that the knife was brand new and whether it would make the sound of it's name as it sliced through the air: Wusthof!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1994126011637135048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fKEzIhwT/WjzRGj7g35P7c9w0Lh6aQgP2+dHQBRjZm25KfY68R9/03N3D/gQYaDWqvTKZELRpHzD0nVXo0BeSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KwPlqQS4SD365OuyzYtLJ6eJsxn9MgvlkLfmYQfRilbuiyCx6bTKhnrXjLFelKQcwg2pxcWKp5aIgtR2sPKycQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/63356.Josh_Kilmer_Purcell">About Josh Kilmer-Purcell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18036629755022365360">Josh Kilmer-Purcell is the New York Times best-selling author of <i>I Am Not Myself These Days: A Memoir</i> (Harper Perennial 2006),<i> The Bucolic Plague: How Two Manhattanites Became Gentlemen Farmers</i> (Harper 2010), and the novel <i>Candy Everybody Wants</i> (Harper Perennial 2008). He and his partner, Brent Ridge, are also the stars of Planet Green's <i>The Fabulous Beekman Boys.</i> Kilmer-Purcell writes a monthly c</span>
  <span id="freeText18036629755022365360" style="display:none">Josh Kilmer-Purcell is the New York Times best-selling author of <i>I Am Not Myself These Days: A Memoir</i> (Harper Perennial 2006),<i> The Bucolic Plague: How Two Manhattanites Became Gentlemen Farmers</i> (Harper 2010), and the novel <i>Candy Everybody Wants</i> (Harper Perennial 2008). He and his partner, Brent Ridge, are also the stars of Planet Green's <i>The Fabulous Beekman Boys.</i> Kilmer-Purcell writes a monthly column for <i>OUT</i> magazine, and contributes to NPR and numerous other publications. He and his partner divide their time between Manhattan and their goat farm in upstate New York, <a href="http://www.beekman1802.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Beekman 1802.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="18036629755022365360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1631-i-am-not-myself-these-days">Quotes from I Am Not Myself T...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I try to make myself realize that I have learned the difference between right and wrong. That there is such a thing as right and wrong. But instead I've learned that these are things - this "right", this "wrong"- these are things that we are told. Simply told to believe. These are things we have not tested. And while most of the things we are told may be true, it is not until we have tested them, taunted them, flaunted them, that we truly know they are right. Or wrong. Or true. Or false. Or somewhere in-the-fucking-between. And I think I know now a little better which is which. And I also know I'll never quit testing this world. I'll never rely on common knowledge. Or common denominators. Or even common sense, for that matter.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/275309-i-try-to-make-myself-realize-that-i-have-learned">27 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I am not an alcoholic. I'm a social catalyst. People pay me to illustrate for other partygoers the chemical process involved in transforming from one persona into another drunker, more fun one. It's a matter of going from dull point A to exciting point B. And I'm a raving success at it. So successful that sometimes I wind up at Mysterious Point C.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/118963-i-am-not-an-alcoholic-i-m-a-social-catalyst-people">22 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/1631-i-am-not-myself-these-days">More quotes&hellip;</a>
